  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_01006f4b-490d-4d28-b153-a96446239ef8'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText3670302554267657593" style="display:none">Jack Reacher is back. <br />The countdown has begun. Get ready for the most exciting 61 hours of your life. #1 "New York Times" bestselling author Lee Child's latest thriller is a ticking time bomb of suspense that builds electric tension on every page. <br />Sixty-one hours. Not a minute to spare. <br />A tour bus crashes in a savage snowstorm and lands Jack Reacher in the middle of a deadly confrontation. In nearby Bolton, South Dakota, one brave woman is standing up for justice in a small town threatened by sinister forces. If she's going to live long enough to testify, she'll need help. Because a killer is coming to Bolton, a coldly proficient assassin who never misses. <br />Reacher's original plan was to keep on moving. But the next 61 hours will change everything. The secrets are deadlier and his enemies are stronger than he could have guessed--but so is the woman whose life he'll risk his own to save. <br />In 61 Hours, Lee Child has written a showdown thriller with an explosive ending that readers will talk about for a long time to come.</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/59371202-dan-flanagan"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/59371202-dan-flanagan">Dan Flanagan</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Jet fuel is not something so flammable that it explodes on contact with something like a flare. It would simply catch fire and burn. It might not even<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Jet fuel is not something so flammable that it explodes on contact with something like a flare. It would simply catch fire and burn. It might not even do that. There's a YouTube video showing that nothing happens when you place a lit match in to a small bowl of jet fuel (what happens is that the jet fuel extinguishes the lit match). But place this jet fuel in an aerosol bottle and spray it onto a lit match and you get something resembling a flame-thrower times one thousand. SO REACHER HAS TIME TO CLIMB OUT OF THE SILO BEFORE GETTING BURNED.<br /><br />You learn on the third page of chapter 3 of the next book (Worth Dying For) that the drunk doctor was able to ascertain that Reacher "damaged every muscle, tendon, and ligament associated with moving your arms" the result of Reacher climbing frantically to get OUT of the silo in time.<br /><br />Then on about page 7 of chapter 23 you read this:<br />"I was in an underground chamber. It caught on fire. There was a STAIR shaft and two VENTILATION shafts. I was lucky. The flames went up the VENTILATION shafts. I was on the stairs so I wasn't burned. But air to feed the fire was coming down the STAIR shaft just as hard as the flames were going back up the VENTILATION shafts. So it was like climbing through a hurricane."<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>

<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    No, the Russian who hired them to kill Plato (not knowing that they chose to set the underground "warehouse" on fire with jet fuel) had previously mad<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    No, the Russian who hired them to kill Plato (not knowing that they chose to set the underground "warehouse" on fire with jet fuel) had previously made a deal with a crooked DEA agent who still had a bit of a conscience. The agreement was to leave the "product" underground and never to attempt distributing it. Which the Russian readily agreed to because he had loftier dreams and plans.....<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7449333393398365680">61 Hours (Jack Reacher, #14), Lee Child<br/><br/>61 Hours is the fourteenth book in the Jack Reacher series written by Lee Child. It is written in the third person, and first published on 18 March 2010. <br/><br/>Set in the town of Bolton, South Dakota, Reacher begins his latest adventure on a wrecked senior citizen tour bus after a near-miss with another motorist leaves the bus spinning on the icy road and trapped in a snowy bank. Immersed in a frozen landscape, Reacher works with local law enforcement to help the</span>
  <span id="freeText7449333393398365680" style="display:none">61 Hours (Jack Reacher, #14), Lee Child<br /><br />61 Hours is the fourteenth book in the Jack Reacher series written by Lee Child. It is written in the third person, and first published on 18 March 2010. <br /><br />Set in the town of Bolton, South Dakota, Reacher begins his latest adventure on a wrecked senior citizen tour bus after a near-miss with another motorist leaves the bus spinning on the icy road and trapped in a snowy bank. Immersed in a frozen landscape, Reacher works with local law enforcement to help the fragile victims. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و چهارم ماه ژانویه سال 2017 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: 61 ساعت (شصت و یک ساعت)؛ نویسنده: لی چایلد؛ مترجم: محمد عباس آبادی؛ تهران، کتابسرای تندیس، 1396، در 519ص؛ شابک 9786001823176؛ فروست: سری جک ریچر، 14؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 21م<br /><br />چهاردهمین کتاب از: سری «جک ریچر»، به قلم: «لی چایلد» با عنوان: «61 ساعت»، که برای نخستین بار در سال 2010 میلادی منتشر شده است؛ <br /><br />داستان، در شهری سرد و پوشیده از برف، به نام: «بولتون»، در «داکوتای جنوبی» می‌گذرد، و با تصادف یک اتوبوس توریستی، که از قضا «ریچر» هم، از مسافران آن است، آغاز می‌شود؛ «ریچر»، پس از ورود به شهر، ذرمییابد یک باند مواد مخدر، در صدد از بین بردن «جانت سالتر» است، چون او شاهد یکی از معاملات آن باند بوده است؛ «جانت سالتر»، برای اینکه زنده بماند، تا شهادت دهد، به یاری نیاز دارد، چرا که قاتلی، در راه «بولتون» است؛ قاتلی کار‌کشته، که تیرش خطا نمی‌رود، و در پی قتل «جانت» است؛ «ریچر»، نخست میاندیشد، که به راه خویش ادامه دهد، و شهر را ترک کند، اما «61 ساعت» بعدی، همه چیز را تغییر می‌دهد. او با رازهای مرگبار، و دشمنانی خطرناک‌تر از آنچه حدس می‌زند، مواجه است...؛ <br /><br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_78971125" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78971125" />
    <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again"><img alt="Jeanette (Again)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304653755p2/796425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78971125?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette (Again)" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again">Jeanette (Again)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=all-fiction">all-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=miss-trees">miss-trees</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78971125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8027338248348306125">I'm going with 3.5 stars on this one. There's only one reason I can't nudge it up to 4 stars, which I'll explain at the end of the review (with plenty of advance warning.)<br/><br/>Jack Reacher novels fall into two categories. One is the big city, ABO, non-stop action, heavy violence thriller such as <i>Gone Tomorrow</i>. The other is the small town, slower-paced, watching and waiting type---more mystery than thriller. <i>61 Hours</i> is in the second category, although it does get pretty exciting later on. I'm cool wi</span>
  <span id="freeText8027338248348306125" style="display:none">I'm going with 3.5 stars on this one. There's only one reason I can't nudge it up to 4 stars, which I'll explain at the end of the review (with plenty of advance warning.)<br /><br />Jack Reacher novels fall into two categories. One is the big city, ABO, non-stop action, heavy violence thriller such as <i>Gone Tomorrow</i>. The other is the small town, slower-paced, watching and waiting type---more mystery than thriller. <i>61 Hours</i> is in the second category, although it does get pretty exciting later on. I'm cool with both kinds, but the adrenaline junkies probably prefer the action-packed ones. <br /><br />A bus accident leaves Jack stranded in the fictional town of Bolton, South Dakota in the dead of winter. Brrrrrr! Cold and getting colder. Snow and ice and wind...and more snow. And of course, the town has problems only Jack can fix. Murders in town, a mysterious abandoned military site a few miles away, a biker in the local prison, and a midget called Plato down in Mexico all combine to give Reacher's solving skills a workout. <br /><br />Less action, but a lot of fun stuff here. I loved the interaction between Jack and the voice on the phone in Washington. Also the discovery of the original purpose behind the military site. Very cool and creepy. And there's a new angle on the old drug running plot element which caught me off guard and then made me laugh at the end with its final effects on the town. We also get to learn a little more about Jack's childhood, thanks to a certain snooper.<br /><br />This concludes the spoiler-free portion of my review. <br /><br />***********WARNING! STOP READING NOW TO AVOID SPOILERS!**************<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />SPOILERS COMING.....<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />The inconclusive ending was frustrating and unsatisfying, so I can't go up to four stars. I don't mind not knowing everything, but we should at least get to find out how Jack escaped from the explosion and see him exiting town with another successful problem taken care of. The last we see of him, he's trying to get out before the flare hits the fuel, and we're left hanging until October. No fair! I think Child made a tactical error with this ending, but I guess now it's all about selling more books more often.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8027338248348306125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2049875514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2049875514" />
    <a title="Anish Kohli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli"><img alt="Anish Kohli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579696384p2/20963257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2049875514?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anish Kohli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anish Kohli" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli">Anish Kohli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440243694" href="/book/show/8228026-61-hours">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2049875514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer875659575651864893"><b>
  <blockquote> He called out, ‘Do you think you can beat me?’ <br/>Reacher called back, ‘Do you think bears shit in the woods?’</blockquote>
</b> Want a straight forward read? Small crisp sentences? Great details? Some ass kicking? Deadpan humor? Riveting storyline and yet easy to put down? A book to work as a filler before you pick the next big series or a tome? Or a book that won’t require the complete attention of your faculties? A kickass lead? Cold hard calculations? Things going boom? <br/><br/>Well, look no further! Lee Child is h</span>
  <span id="freeText875659575651864893" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote> He called out, ‘Do you think you can beat me?’ <br>Reacher called back, ‘Do you think bears shit in the woods?’</blockquote>
</b> Want a straight forward read? Small crisp sentences? Great details? Some ass kicking? Deadpan humor? Riveting storyline and yet easy to put down? A book to work as a filler before you pick the next big series or a tome? Or a book that won’t require the complete attention of your faculties? A kickass lead? Cold hard calculations? Things going boom? <br><br>Well, look no further! Lee Child is here to serve all of these needs thorough Jack Reacher, an ex-military police veteran, who lives the life of a hermit. Why, you ask? Freedom, Bitch! <blockquote>
  <b>“He had said what needed to be said, and he hadn’t cared who he said it to. He had done what needed to be done, and he hadn’t cared who he did it to.”</b>
</blockquote> Its book #14 and I think we’re way past the point of explaining things in depth. If you have even a small thing for Reacher books, you’ll end up really liking this one! I have stuck around with this series for quite a while now and this book has to be one of the best in the series for me personally.<br><br>Jack Reacher books come in varieties. They can be first person POV or third person POV. They can be completely action packed or slow burns with more of a head scratching element. Variety! <br>This book is 3rd person POV and more of a head scratching one. But still pretty straight forward and there is a big BOOM towards the end! <br>Reacher, as is the norm, finds himself in trouble for no reason and we all know he isn’t one to back down. Stuck in the town of Bolton (Ramsey?) by accident, figuratively and literally. He now must solve the curious case that Bolton PD have going on bcz well, that’s what Reacher does. He is the Judge, Jury and Executioner right after he is done playing the Investigator, Evidence Analyst, Defense Analyst, Firearms Expert, Threats Analyst, Security Advisor, a Courtroom and pretty much everything else! He is a Dog with a Bone! Dog on a scent and he won’t stop till he’s done. He’s got his own rules. He’s got his own standards and his own measure of things. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510209906ra/24399011.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>No he isn’t. At best, he is an obsessing asshole who can’t let things go. I think Reacher is the closest thing I have read to what you can call an Anti-Hero. He doesn’t qualify, I think, but he gets close! Real close.<br><br>The highlight of this book, for me, are two things:<br>1.	Even if for a moment, Reacher is sulky and low. Almost beaten. Something he rectifies and gets going again but that makes his character better. Not a tough guy through and through. A guy who plays tough. Sounds better.<br><br>2.	I think for the first time in this series, Lee Child has ended a book on a cliffhanger! All his books are self-contained but this time, seems like the author is in a mind of shaking things up. And all though it isn’t much of a cliffhanger but it is still there and that’s good. Now I guess I will be reading the next one sooner than I thought.<br><br>I ended up dragging this book for months due to other more immersive reads and obviously due to all the ass-kicking real life doled out to me but this is actually a quick read despite the number of pages. Most people find or think Reacher books are slow and repetitive. I think that’s what actually makes them good and true to the character of Jack Reacher. He is a sloth until he actually has a reason to expend his energy. He is calculative and analyzing till he needs to act on it.<br><br>This series, for me, is like a guilty read. I always resort to a Reacher book in times of despair and times when I feel like I might hit a slump. They keep me reading but never really ask for all my attention. And they always make me smile bcz it’s always amazing to see how much of an ass Reacher can be!<br><br>So go on, try him out and you might like him. But take a piece of advice, you do not mess with Reacher. Ever! Period!<br><br>PS: Casting Tom Cruise as Reacher? Dean knows how I feel!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467299043ra/19577119.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="875659575651864893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2375320003" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Alp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26653561-alp"><img alt="Alp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462791280p2/26653561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2375320003?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alp" href="/user/show/26653561-alp">Alp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2375320003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer132852156658886895"><b>4.25 stars</b><br/><br/>Another unputdownable read by Lee Child.<br/><br/>As usual, this one didn't disappoint. I liked how suspenseful and gripping the story was. I thoroughly enjoyed reading this installment, the real page-turner, from start to finish.<br/><br/>My only minor complaint is that the action scene near the end of the book lacked a bit of excitement and intensity. I was just expecting something a little more action-packed and heart-pounding. <br/><br/>Nevertheless, it was a good and engaging read with a clever plot. If you’re</span>
  <span id="freeText132852156658886895" style="display:none"><b>4.25 stars</b><br /><br />Another unputdownable read by Lee Child.<br /><br />As usual, this one didn't disappoint. I liked how suspenseful and gripping the story was. I thoroughly enjoyed reading this installment, the real page-turner, from start to finish.<br /><br />My only minor complaint is that the action scene near the end of the book lacked a bit of excitement and intensity. I was just expecting something a little more action-packed and heart-pounding. <br /><br />Nevertheless, it was a good and engaging read with a clever plot. If you’re a crime-mystery/thriller/suspense fan, then you shouldn’t miss out on this series.<br /><br /><br />**This book can be read as a standalone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="132852156658886895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148843751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16750053995424882437">I had to laugh. Those of us in the thriller game talk about building suspense with the "ticking clock": a hard deadline that the characters are up against. If they don't make it, all is lost. So what does Lee Child do? He imbeds an almost literal ticking clock in every chapter, ending each one with the reminder that there are "X hours to go." It's such an obvious device that it's like the magician showing you how the trick is done, but it still works-- you still gasp and chuckle with delight as </span>
  <span id="freeText16750053995424882437" style="display:none">I had to laugh. Those of us in the thriller game talk about building suspense with the "ticking clock": a hard deadline that the characters are up against. If they don't make it, all is lost. So what does Lee Child do? He imbeds an almost literal ticking clock in every chapter, ending each one with the reminder that there are "X hours to go." It's such an obvious device that it's like the magician showing you how the trick is done, but it still works-- you still gasp and chuckle with delight as you see the trick pulled off. <br /><br />The secret hidden beneath the snowbound wastes near Bolton, South Dakota, is one that a very scary villain is willing to kill for (or, if necessary, torture, mutilate, cripple, then kill for). Reacher's immediate problem, however, is keeping a flinty old lady alive after she witnesses a drug deal that implicates the minions of said nasty villain. More I will not reveal, except to make one observation: you do NOT want to make Jack Reacher mad. Ever. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16750053995424882437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6630473467947254031">Book 14 in the Jack Reacher series.<br/><br/>This starts as a really slow burn that culminates in an inferno of volcanic proportions.<br/><br/>After a bus accident, which Jack is travelling on, in the middle of nowhere, well not nowhere, Bolton South Dakota to be exact, in the middle of a wind blasted freezing winter, an accident that renders the bus inoperable Jack finds himself the unwitting guest of Bolton’s Assistant Chief of Police. It soon becomes apparent that all is not well in Bolton. A biker clan has take</span>
  <span id="freeText6630473467947254031" style="display:none">Book 14 in the Jack Reacher series.<br /><br />This starts as a really slow burn that culminates in an inferno of volcanic proportions.<br /><br />After a bus accident, which Jack is travelling on, in the middle of nowhere, well not nowhere, Bolton South Dakota to be exact, in the middle of a wind blasted freezing winter, an accident that renders the bus inoperable Jack finds himself the unwitting guest of Bolton’s Assistant Chief of Police. It soon becomes apparent that all is not well in Bolton. A biker clan has taken up residence on the periphery of Bolton and their current business endeavour is the production of methamphetamine. This, as you can imagine, is cause for a great deal of friction between the locals and the biker gang.<br /><br />To make matters worse a local stalwart witnessed something that will get her killed. The local police are hard pressed to give the witness around the clock protection. So Jack being Jack he puts his hand up to protect the witness, a dear old lady called Janet Salter.<br /><br />Add to the mix a psychopathic Mexican drug Lord who is orchestrating the death of certain Bolton denizens from a thousand miles away. <br /><br />This story took awhile to really get going but once it does ‘kaboom’<br /><br />For me the only downside in the story was that from early in the story the local villain was just a bit too obvious.<br /><br />But for all that another terrific read from Lee Child.<br /><br />A recommended 4 star read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6630473467947254031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150939848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15300189271071461398">After reading <em>61 Hours</em>, I'm left with one burning question. Does Jack Reacher ever brush his teeth?<br/><br/>Lee Child goes into a lot of detail about how his hulking protagonist drifts around the United States with literally no possessions -- not even a backpack -- and how he buys a new set of clothes every week and throws away the old set. But does he ever brush his teeth? Does he bathe? Does he shave? If he doesn't shave, does he have a beard? He's not described with one.<br/><br/>If Child were more vague about </span>
  <span id="freeText15300189271071461398" style="display:none">After reading <em>61 Hours</em>, I'm left with one burning question. Does Jack Reacher ever brush his teeth?<br /><br />Lee Child goes into a lot of detail about how his hulking protagonist drifts around the United States with literally no possessions -- not even a backpack -- and how he buys a new set of clothes every week and throws away the old set. But does he ever brush his teeth? Does he bathe? Does he shave? If he doesn't shave, does he have a beard? He's not described with one.<br /><br />If Child were more vague about Reacher's life on the road, I'd never even consider these things, but he goes into such detail about Reacher's clothing-buying habits that he creates a whole new set of questions.<br /><br />He goes into detail about a lot of things. Sometimes he's almost like someone with Asperger's Syndrome. He describes tire ruts in snowy, icy roads so often in this novel that it's nearly fetishistic.<br /><br /><em>61 Hours</em> has a built-in stopwatch. As Jack Reacher attempts to protect the life of an elderly woman who is to testify against a drug gang, everything leads toward some nebulous event that is going to occur 61 hours after a bus crash lands him in the small town of Bolton, South Dakota, in the middle of subzero weather and a snowstorm. Many chapters end with the line, "Five minutes to xx in the morning. Xx hours to go."<br /><br /><em>61 Hours</em> starts out strong, but nearly three days is a long time to keep your audience engaged, and too much of the middle three-fifths of this book feels like padding.<br /><br />The last 50 pages are pretty good, but not spectacular. Jack Reacher is a two-dimensional good guy facing a one-dimensional bad guy, so this book never involved me enough to feel as if I couldn't wait to finish it.<br /><br />I like a lot of Child's attitude and his way with a thriller, but so far for me his series hasn't met the expectations set by all the raves from his rabid fans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15300189271071461398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89326405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89326405" />
    <a title="Mandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/649999-mandy"><img alt="Mandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239924307p2/649999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89326405?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy" href="/user/show/649999-mandy">Mandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780593057063" href="/book/show/6735719-61-hours">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/649999-mandy?shelf=four-stars">four-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/649999-mandy?shelf=lee-child">lee-child</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/649999-mandy?shelf=arc-reviewers-copy">arc-reviewers-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89326405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11777950260981264459"><b>(Disclaimer: This review is written by someone who is a huge Lee Child/Jack Reacher fan. I will try and not let the bias creep in too much. Having said that, this book did not disappoint and I dare you to read it and find otherwise.)</b><br/><br/>The clock is ticking....61 hours….enough time for Reacher to become fully embroiled in another action-packed adventure….you betcha!<br/><br/><i>61 Hours</i> is Lee Child’s latest book, the 14th for the Jack Reacher series. Reacher is an ex-military police officer who doesn’t really c</span>
  <span id="freeText11777950260981264459" style="display:none"><b>(Disclaimer: This review is written by someone who is a huge Lee Child/Jack Reacher fan. I will try and not let the bias creep in too much. Having said that, this book did not disappoint and I dare you to read it and find otherwise.)</b><br /><br />The clock is ticking....61 hours….enough time for Reacher to become fully embroiled in another action-packed adventure….you betcha!<br /><br /><i>61 Hours</i> is Lee Child’s latest book, the 14th for the Jack Reacher series. Reacher is an ex-military police officer who doesn’t really call anywhere home; carries very little, even opting to buy his clothes on a need-to-buy basis whilst discarding his old clothes; carries a toothbrush and passport and if possible nothing else; is strong, powerful and has quite an intelligent mind. Reacher is a man who can fix problems, more often than not, problems that don’t have anything to do with him…until he gets involved. <br /><br />The latest setting Reacher finds himself in is a small town in South Dakota. Being one who often finds transport and jumps onboard, not necessarily caring where he ends up but just heading “somewhere”, Reacher manages to get a ride with a group of old age men and women on a tour bus. Not Reacher’s usual fare but never fear, this is not the opening of a novel that will proceed to describe long chats over cups of tea and games of bingo. There is a horror snowstorm on foot when the group passes through South Dakota. Unfortunately there is an accident and they are all holed up in the small town for a couple of days. Fate works in mysterious ways though as it is not unfortunate for the law abiding citizens of the town, now they have Jack Reacher at their fingertips and Andrew Peterson (town policeman) intends to ask for Reacher’s help with a few things.<br /><br />Something big is going on in this small town. A little old lady is under police protection, due to stand trial as a witness to a drug deal in court. There’s a strange building out in the middle of nowhere. There’s Plato, a big man in the business of drugs, a small man in stature, a man controlling events from Mexico and this man doesn’t care who gets hurt in the process. There’s something not quite right happening, a few peculiar events here and there, a few deaths here and there, a few things that just don’t add up. Well, Jack’s back and you can bet he’ll do his damnedest to find the answers….after all, it’s bloody freezing and he needs to do something to stay warm. The clock is ticking….61 hours….will this be enough time for Reacher to be the hero we know he is?<br /><br />I read <i>61 Hours</i> whilst I was on holiday in Bali. Absolutely fantastic holiday read. I didn’t want to put it down; I just had to find out what was going to happen next. As always with Lee Child’s books I am engrossed from the first sentence and if you want to interrupt me whilst I’m reading you had better have a really good reason to do so. Mr Child just knows how to write to keep the reader entertained and interested. His main character Jack Reacher is a favourite of mine and Lee Child is my favourite author. What more can I say? His novels are always page-turners and once they’re finished you wish you hadn’t read so fast because now you have to wait for a new book to come out. Lucky for us <i>61 Hours</i> ends with <i>
  <b>“To be continued 30/9/10”</b>
</i> so we have two books this year! I cannot wait until the 30th of September.<br /><br />If you haven’t read any Lee Child books I strongly advise you to do so, immediately, if not sooner. Be warned though, once you start you won’t be able to stop and you will be just like the rest of us hanging out for the new release every year. There should be a warning on Lee Child’s books….highly addictive!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11777950260981264459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_114231049" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114231049" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3046073-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294870691p2/3046073.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114231049?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/3046073-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114231049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer977748043349918305">I was bitterly disappointed in this book. Bitter, because I am a huge Jack Reacher fan and have never been as disappointed in one of his books as I was in this one.<br/><br/>First, the setting. I found the cold interesting at first, because I've never been in such extreme cold before... until I realized that the author was going to go on, and on, and on about it. Each minute Reacher was colder than the previous minute. And we knew this because we were told it in almost every paragraph. Every description w</span>
  <span id="freeText977748043349918305" style="display:none">I was bitterly disappointed in this book. Bitter, because I am a huge Jack Reacher fan and have never been as disappointed in one of his books as I was in this one.<br /><br />First, the setting. I found the cold interesting at first, because I've never been in such extreme cold before... until I realized that the author was going to go on, and on, and on about it. Each minute Reacher was colder than the previous minute. And we knew this because we were told it in almost every paragraph. Every description was the same. White. Snow. Cold. Some ice thrown in for fun. Very dull.<br /><br />Second, the action. Or lack thereof. Usually Reacher books are full of non-stop action, and fans of the series come to expect it. I know I do. Seeing how Reacher reacts in crazy circumstances is part of the fun of reading his books. 61 Hours, in that regard, was like watching paint dry. Nothing happened. Lots of talk, but no action. By the time you find a little bit of action in the very last pages of the book, it's too little &amp; too late.<br /><br />Third, the plot. Could there have been a more dull, plodding plot? Usually Jack Reacher books are full of twists and turns. You think you know what's going to happen, then something else happens and you realize you were way off - usually this happens at least 4 or 5 times in one Reacher book. Not so with this one. I guessed "whodunit" in the first 1/4 of the book and ended up being right. I can't remember this ever happening in another Reacher book. Therefore, I found the rest of the book slow and frustrating as I waited for Reacher to figure it out too. Another note about the plot - I found the whole time thing very annoying. We're told multiple times in each chapter how many hours/minutes were left in the countdown (as the title suggests, it started with 61 hours).<br /><br />Fourth, the ending. I won't divulge anything or spoil anything for someone wanting to read this book... I will merely say that when I closed the book I was disgusted. Mostly disgusted at myself for wasting my time reading this book.<br /><br />I never thought I'd be writing such a harsh review of a book in one of my favorite series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="977748043349918305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549400156i/27020211._SY540_.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Jack Reacher Poster<br>

  <u>61 hours</u>
</b> - is the title of the book)<br><br>Jack Reacher (the famous drifter &amp; ex-military policeman) is traveling on a “Bus” stranded on a icy hill after almost being hit by a car &amp; helps the people in the Bus escape/survive. The busy Town, it’s large 60 cell Prison, needs more guards, a small police dept. asks for his help to solve a crime.<br><br>Reacher’s experience with “South Dakota’s weather in the winter was not famously hospitable” to survive. Winters cold with high temperatures averaging below freezing &amp; low temperatures averaging below 10 °F (−12 °C) in most of the state.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Reacher needs to find a link from the murdered Lawyer in the Prison Parking lot, to a Town Police murder, Bolton Politician scam to get Prison funds &amp; finding a dead biker? <br>He needs to find the relation between Bolton resident and/or Criminal leader, storing a <b>”meth” drug</b> (Methylated amphetamine). <br><br>Why is <b>Janet Salter</b>, the major witness &amp; can Reacher protect her? Where is this South American “Godfather” drug character living in Mexico?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551783543i/27156517._SX540_.jpg" width="260" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>A movie with Tom Cruise, starring as Reacher was reviewed again<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The hour “chapter” countdown used in the book is nice, e.g. <b>Chapter 60 hours</b> to go, <b>Chapter 59 hours</b> to go, 58, 57, etc. until 2 hours to go &amp; the end of the book. And nice with few characters to track.<br><br>Like other Reacher books - he travels with nothing, “always buys new”.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_137327387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137327387" />
    <a title="Richard Hunt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3285566-richard-hunt"><img alt="Richard Hunt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300309544p2/3285566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137327387?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Hunt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Hunt" href="/user/show/3285566-richard-hunt">Richard Hunt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137327387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4383170271191215199">I have been a big Lee Child fan over the past few years. However in my opinion this was the slowest most painful reading experience i have had in a very long time. The Reacher character is becoming tired and book after book the author seems to be rewriting the back story so that once you have heard his history once you will see it in every book. This is a plausible point, as not everyone will read all of the Jack Reacher books and they need to learn about the protagonist.<br/>However in 61 Hours you </span>
  <span id="freeText4383170271191215199" style="display:none">I have been a big Lee Child fan over the past few years. However in my opinion this was the slowest most painful reading experience i have had in a very long time. The Reacher character is becoming tired and book after book the author seems to be rewriting the back story so that once you have heard his history once you will see it in every book. This is a plausible point, as not everyone will read all of the Jack Reacher books and they need to learn about the protagonist.<br />However in 61 Hours you are given a lengthy character back history half way through the book, which is a poor edit, as you really need this earlier in the book so you can invest emotion and sympathise with the main character. It seems inserted as an afterthought. Also the book could have been cut by a third and not have detracted from the story at all. Seems Lee completed the book, thought it was too short and then during the editing phase bulked up the book by putting boring descriptions in which detract from what could have been a reasonable book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4383170271191215199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_917257702" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/917257702" />
    <a title="Cortez Law III" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14167873-cortez-law-iii"><img alt="Cortez Law III" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398195731p2/14167873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/917257702?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cortez Law III" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cortez Law III" href="/user/show/14167873-cortez-law-iii">Cortez Law III</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer917257702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17310586769109478236">Knock The Chill Off With This Thriller<br/><br/>First off, let me say that if I had any notion of a vacation in winter, I’m not going to South Dakota. Lee Child’s thriller, 61 Hours, finds Jack Reacher the victim of a bus accident in sub- zero weather along a lonely stretch of highway with a busload of senior citizens. Being the Good Samaritan that he is, he assists the bus driver as much as he can as well as the other passengers. Takes a bit, but they finally get the help they need, which leads them to t</span>
  <span id="freeText17310586769109478236" style="display:none">Knock The Chill Off With This Thriller<br /><br />First off, let me say that if I had any notion of a vacation in winter, I’m not going to South Dakota. Lee Child’s thriller, 61 Hours, finds Jack Reacher the victim of a bus accident in sub- zero weather along a lonely stretch of highway with a busload of senior citizens. Being the Good Samaritan that he is, he assists the bus driver as much as he can as well as the other passengers. Takes a bit, but they finally get the help they need, which leads them to the town of Bolton, SD.<br />As is his custom, or better said Mr. Child’s custom, this unexpected detour lands Reacher in the midst of a brewing storm, literally on two counts: One, an even nastier weather system is on the way to make its acquaintance with the locals, not too much skin off their noses as they’re used to it for the most part. Moreover, number two, a stealthy plot beneath the frozen city’s surfaces churns in town and the much warmer south of the border locale of Mexico. Trouble’s coming and someone wants a few people dead that are impediments to rather lucrative and quite interesting loot. That loot borders on the legal/illegal gray area and blurred line. Read this story and you’ll understand that statement.<br /><br />Without divulging too much for those who haven’t yet indulged in this Child thriller, Reacher’s chief concern is someone hard pressed to defend herself against some sly opposition who only want her dead and out of their way. I think what amazed me the most with this book was how Lee Child painted such a picture of the landscape that felt as if you’re actually in that environment. How he sustained that with his prose gifts and hooked me in with the suspense that built with the unstoppable countdown, hence the title, 61 Hours, is to read a true master at his craft. Writers remember to include weather in your stories. This is a lesson in how the surroundings can be a character. So anyway, when the clock inevitably strikes twelve if you will, a whole lot of stuff hits the fan, the ceiling, the roof and everything else in sight.<br /><br />The characters are well drawn especially the local towns people. Considering the ‘story’s’ construct, perhaps Reacher’s opposition wasn’t as strong as in other adventures. But Child creates a rather ingenious character that fits the ‘landscape’ construct that makes for a compelling mano-a-mano battle. In addition, a very interesting but personal Reacher subplot further plumbs the depth of his character for his many fans to contemplate. It left me wondering is it possible for Jack Reacher to, let’s just say, stay in one place for a bit or aka, settle down like most of humanity. Well, here’s hoping against that one. Hey, no offense to the flirty professional person in question. However, we fans of Jack Reacher accept him as a direct, spare, brilliant deductive reasoning, take no prisoners, human Terminator. Look more than forward to losing myself in the next Reacher adventure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17310586769109478236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262214255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18037742031372386213">Not enough action. Reacher did some unsmart things. Incomplete ending. But, because I like hanging out with Reacher it was ok.<br/><br/>STORY BRIEF:<br/>Reacher is on a bus. Due to winter weather he is stranded in Bolton, S. Dakota. Local police are guarding an elderly woman who witnessed a drug deal. Reacher decides to help protect her.<br/><br/>A biker gang has been living near Bolton in an abandoned army compound. The police believe they have been selling drugs (meth). The biker gang works for Plato, a Mexican drug l</span>
  <span id="freeText18037742031372386213" style="display:none">Not enough action. Reacher did some unsmart things. Incomplete ending. But, because I like hanging out with Reacher it was ok.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />Reacher is on a bus. Due to winter weather he is stranded in Bolton, S. Dakota. Local police are guarding an elderly woman who witnessed a drug deal. Reacher decides to help protect her.<br /><br />A biker gang has been living near Bolton in an abandoned army compound. The police believe they have been selling drugs (meth). The biker gang works for Plato, a Mexican drug lord who does very bad things to people.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />Not the best Reacher story. There were a few stupid decisions that bothered me. For example, police personnel asked Reacher to do some things for them. Each time this took Reacher away from protecting the witness which Reacher should have planned for. That was out of character for him.<br /><br />Other Reacher books had more thriller and suspense. This was mostly noodling through the mystery. There was almost no action until the very end of the book. And that was not enough. I’d like to tell you the number of bad guys that Reacher took out in this book, but I won’t, to avoid spoilers. I’ll just say that his count was extremely low compared to other books, which made it less fun. <br /><br />I was very disappointed that the author DID NOT FINISH THE STORY! I believe the author ran out of time or hit a writer’s block. The reader doesn’t know if Reacher is dead or alive or how he survived if alive. (Hint: We know he lives because there are sequels.) The sequel “Worth Dying For” begins a couple days after “61 Hours.” WDF has a brief comment about how Reacher survived at the end of 61H. But it wasn’t enough for me.<br /><br />I loved the short back story about the military doing psychological research on little kids. They filmed kids’ reactions while watching a movie with a monster. When the monster appeared on the screen all the kids leaned back in their seats with fear on their faces - except for 6-year-old Reacher. He was the only kid who reacted with aggression instead of fear. He had drawn his switchblade open in less than a second and was leaning forward in his seat to attack the monster. Another LOL for me.<br /><br />NARRATOR:<br />The narrator Dick Hill was very good.	<br /><br />DATA:<br />Unabridged audiobook reading time: 13 hrs and 11 mins. Swearing language: I don’t recall any. Sexual content: none. Setting: current day mostly S. Dakota with a little Mexico. Book copyright: 2010. Genre: mystery suspense thriller. Ending: mostly good but unfinished.<br /><br />THE SERIES:							<br />Following is a list of the Jack Reacher books in order with my ratings. All the books could be read as stand-alones, but I suggest reading them in order, maybe saving the lower rated ones for last.<br /><br />4 ½ stars. Killing Floor (#1)<br />4 stars. Die Trying (#2)<br />4 stars. Tripwire (#3)<br />2 ½ stars. Running Blind (#4)<br />4 stars. Echo Burning (#5)					<br />3 ½ stars. Without Fail (#6)<br />4 stars. Persuader (#7)<br />3 stars. The Enemy (#8)<br />4 ½ stars. One Shot (#9)<br />3 stars. The Hard Way (#10)<br />3 ½ stars. Bad Luck and Trouble (#11)<br />2 stars. Nothing To Lose (#12) too many low ratings<br />4 stars. Gone Tomorrow (#13)<br />3 stars. 61 Hours (#14)<br />4 ½ stars. Worth Dying For (#15)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6558535101493507741">I've read every Lee Child book there is and adore Jack Reacher. You have to feel for the guy, as he just wants to keep his head down, stay out of trouble, and keep moving. Yet he keeps getting pulled into situations where he has no choice but to help strangers, as he can't walk away from doing the right thing. That's why I love Reacher, as he's one of the good guys.<br/><br/>This is another great Reacher book and if you've enjoyed the others, I'm pretty sure you'll like this one as well. The only thing I </span>
  <span id="freeText6558535101493507741" style="display:none">I've read every Lee Child book there is and adore Jack Reacher. You have to feel for the guy, as he just wants to keep his head down, stay out of trouble, and keep moving. Yet he keeps getting pulled into situations where he has no choice but to help strangers, as he can't walk away from doing the right thing. That's why I love Reacher, as he's one of the good guys.<br /><br />This is another great Reacher book and if you've enjoyed the others, I'm pretty sure you'll like this one as well. The only thing I didn't care for was the countdown throughout the book, letting us know how many hours were left. Could have done without that, but it's a small thing and don't think it would bother anyone else but me.<br /><br />Child is a very good writer, and Reacher is a very good character. You know that if you pick up one of his books, you're going to get a good story. Great pacing, good plot, and believable characters. Was a little surprised by the ending, which I hadn't seen coming, and can't wait to see what Child has up his sleeve for the next book! Highly recommended!<br /></span>

<div id="review_101968327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101968327" />
    <a title="Maddy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1298544-maddy"><img alt="Maddy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231701631p2/1298544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101968327?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddy" href="/user/show/1298544-maddy">Maddy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1298544-maddy?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101968327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8267741359684702138">PROTAGONIST: Jack Reacher<br/>SETTING: South Dakota <br/>SERIES: #14 of 14<br/>RATING: 3.5<br/><br/>In the fourteenth book of the Jack Reacher series, our peripatetic adventurer finds himself on a bus filled with senior citizens that has just slid into a ditch in snowy South Dakota. It will be a few days before a replacement bus will be able to continue their journey, so everyone on the bus is taken into the homes of the inhabitants of Bolton, SD. As you might expect, Reacher is not spending his time counting the cows d</span>
  <span id="freeText8267741359684702138" style="display:none">PROTAGONIST: Jack Reacher<br />SETTING: South Dakota <br />SERIES: #14 of 14<br />RATING: 3.5<br /><br />In the fourteenth book of the Jack Reacher series, our peripatetic adventurer finds himself on a bus filled with senior citizens that has just slid into a ditch in snowy South Dakota. It will be a few days before a replacement bus will be able to continue their journey, so everyone on the bus is taken into the homes of the inhabitants of Bolton, SD. As you might expect, Reacher is not spending his time counting the cows during the wait. Instead, he is immediately recruited to help the local police department solve a murder. The police in this town have a lot on their plate due to the recent construction of a prison that has swelled their population and resulted in an influx of visitors. It’s all a bit dysfunctional, as the police department has expanded dramatically; and there’s a mixture of old and new employees who aren’t all very skilled at what they do. <br /><br />One important assignment that the police have is to protect an elderly resident, Mrs. Salter, who is the sole witness willing to testify against a local biker gang. There’s one problem with the situation, an agreement with the prison that if their siren sounds, every police officer in the town will respond to the call. If this were to happen, Mrs. Salter would be left alone and likely killed. Reacher steps in to assist. This is one instance where the miserable weather is a help, in that the only approach of a possible assassin would be from the front of the home, since the entire property is snowbound.<br /><br />But bigger things are brewing. Throughout the book, there is a countdown, beginning at 61 hours, for something that is going to happen, although we don’t know what that is. It seems to involve a remote local site that is currently being used by a biker gang likely making meth, who mysteriously vacate one evening, and a Mexican drug lord. The entire countdown premise was a flawed concept for me. Normally, this device is very suspenseful, in that we are expecting some cataclysmic event to happen which is generally foiled by the hero at 3 seconds to go. But in this case, there is no indication of what the event will be, so the reader is unable to build a sense of horror at what might happen. In addition, the countdown is conducted continuously throughout the book—Five minutes to eleven in the evening. Fifty-three hours to go…..Five minutes to six in the morning. Thirty-seven hours to go. This rapidly became irritating.<br /><br />On the positive side, Child does a fabulous job of describing the barren, freezing setting. Even someone as intrepid as Reacher has a hard time functioning in such an unforgiving environment. There’s also a hint that he may be ready to invest in a real relationship. The possible love interest currently holds the same position in the Army that Reacher did in the past, which leads to some interesting insights into Jack’s history. <br /><br />Child has also changed the formula a bit. No females were bedded in this book, which was a nice change. Jack actually reaches some incorrect conclusions about various events. And the conclusion is unresolved, with a cliff hanger ending. Even without that, I’d be anxiously awaiting Book 15, as this series is always on my Must Read list.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8267741359684702138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2370752835" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2370752835" />
    <a title="Book Addict Shaun" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7403283-book-addict-shaun"><img alt="Book Addict Shaun" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541433885p2/7403283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2370752835?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Addict Shaun" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Addict Shaun" href="/user/show/7403283-book-addict-shaun">Book Addict Shaun</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553825565" href="/book/show/7962896-61-hours">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2370752835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14619021747127456666">61 Hours might be one of my least favourites in the series so far, but it was still an enjoyable read the ending saved the story for me. Once again Jack Reacher finds himself on a bus heading through the middle of nowhere. This time it’s South Dakota where the temperature outside is below freezing, and the bus he has hitched a ride on almost crashes. When help arrives from the local town, Reacher heads straight on in to his latest shitstorm. <br/><br/>After fourteen novels Lee Child still writes a grippin</span>
  <span id="freeText14619021747127456666" style="display:none">61 Hours might be one of my least favourites in the series so far, but it was still an enjoyable read the ending saved the story for me. Once again Jack Reacher finds himself on a bus heading through the middle of nowhere. This time it’s South Dakota where the temperature outside is below freezing, and the bus he has hitched a ride on almost crashes. When help arrives from the local town, Reacher heads straight on in to his latest shitstorm. <br /><br />After fourteen novels Lee Child still writes a gripping tale but there are similarities to be drawn with the earlier Reacher novels. There is some repetitiveness here. Reacher coming to the rescue, saving everybody and heading off at the end of the story for his next adventure. Though the ending here for Reacher isn’t as clear as normal. 61 Hours takes places across those 61 hours and you’d expect the story to be action-packed because of that, but it isn’t. Instead it’s a real slow burner, I found myself glazing over certain parts and with knowing the real action wasn’t going to arrive until the 61st hour, it made the rest of the story feel quite dull. <br /><br />A lot of my enjoyment in these books also comes from the characters Reacher spends time with in the story. The ones here didn’t have much to offer and the storyline of the elderly lady refusing to enter witness protection just bored me, I’d rather read about Reacher getting his rocks off again than him being psychoanalysed by an old woman because of his refusal to carry a bag around with him. I love small town settings and the one here was again well-imagined, and the plot had the usual twists and turns you expect from this series, though with one twist being a complete and utter cliche. There was one character that stood out and who offered further insight into Reacher’s character and that’s a woman named Susan who is currently doing the job Reacher did back before he left the army. His scenes on the phone with her were probably some of the most insightful in the book. <br /><br />As said in my review of Gone Tomorrow, I can’t see myself ever not enjoying a Reacher novel, but some I will like less than others and that was the case with 61 Hours. It’s a good instalment into the series however it isn’t one I’d recommend new readers pick up first. Onwards and upwards we go as I continue with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14619021747127456666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_393852177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393852177" />
    <a title="Robin Webster" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7548247-robin-webster"><img alt="Robin Webster" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476215308p2/7548247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393852177?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin Webster" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin Webster" href="/user/show/7548247-robin-webster">Robin Webster</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393852177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6238902331569701196">61 Hours is the first book I have read by Lee Child. All his books feature the all action hero Jack Reacher who was drummed out of a military elite unit some years before and now seems to live a rootless existence, moving from place to place getting involved in all kinds of situations. This book finds him stranded in a small town in South Dakota in mid-winter, after the bus he is travelling on crashes on an icy road. He then gets drawn into trying to protect a vulnerable witness from being murde</span>
  <span id="freeText6238902331569701196" style="display:none">61 Hours is the first book I have read by Lee Child. All his books feature the all action hero Jack Reacher who was drummed out of a military elite unit some years before and now seems to live a rootless existence, moving from place to place getting involved in all kinds of situations. This book finds him stranded in a small town in South Dakota in mid-winter, after the bus he is travelling on crashes on an icy road. He then gets drawn into trying to protect a vulnerable witness from being murdered on the orders of a ruthless gangster called Plato. Plato is based in Mexico and controls a drug ring that is run by a community of bikers who live at a local disused airfield. It is difficult to discuss the plot any further without giving away spoilers.<br /> I really like Lee Child’s style of writing. He is very descriptive with regard to both the setting and environment. Most of the action happens in the latter half of the book. However, the writer does keep you hooked because despite the predictability of part of the plot, there are some unexpected twists. This book was a nice easy enjoyable light read ideal for taking on holiday. It’s never going to win the Booker Prize but once you have read one of his books I get the feeling you will know exactly what you are going to get with the next one, and as a guy that likes all action hero thriller, that is fine by me.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6238902331569701196" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_80747254" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80747254" />
    <a title="Dewey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1164893-dewey"><img alt="Dewey" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80747254?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dewey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dewey" href="/user/show/1164893-dewey">Dewey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780593057063" href="/book/show/6735719-61-hours">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80747254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1191635743927483832">Lee Child at his best. Jack Reacher is stranded in a small South Dakota town due to a snowstorm and as usual manages to find his help is needed. A little old lady witness to a drug deal is being protected from being killed by a Mexican drug lord is the basis of the novel. Jack assists the local Police Department protecting her and investigating the usual murders that seek out Reacher. This is one of my favorite Jack Reacher novels. The pacing was good, high suspense, some surprises. Loved it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>
